2/23/23, 4:10 PM - Bamiche: @⁨ozoiloeugeneokwudili⁩ pending when the proper scale is available for weighing the pigs, please let's use this method to estimate their weight
2/23/23, 4:18 PM - ozoiloeugeneokwudili: Seen, but still studying what you have sent to me
2/23/23, 4:21 PM - Bamiche: *Steps* 

 *1.* Measure the heart length (in meters)

 *2.* Heart length x Heart length for example 1.2m x 1.2m = 1.44 meters 

 *3.* Measure the body length. From the ears to the tail for example 1.02 meters

Constant (kg) 69.3 

 *Calculation* 

Pig weight = heart length x body length x constant (69.3)

 *Our example* 

1.44 x 1.02 x 69.3 = 101.7kg

4/18/23, 3:09 PM - Bamiche: *ASF Awareness* 

Hello all, I will be doing a 9 part ASF awareness series to familiarize us on how the disease is spread and how we can limit behaviors which cause it. 

Please this is for the entire team, so everyone linked to our project should get this information 

Thank you
4/18/23, 3:10 PM - Bamiche: African swine fever (ASF) is a highly contagious viral disease that affects domestic and wild pigs. It can cause severe economic losses in pig populations and the pork industry. Here are some preventive measures that can help prevent the spread of African swine fever:

 *---------------------------------------* 
1. Biosecurity: Implement strict biosecurity measures to prevent the entry of ASF virus into your pig farm. This includes controlling access to your farm, using foot baths or disinfection mats at entry points, and restricting the movement of people, vehicles, and equipment in and out of the farm.

 *---------------------------------------* 

2. Quarantine and testing: Quarantine and test new pigs before introducing them to your farm to ensure that they are free from ASF virus. This includes isolating new pigs for a period of time and testing them for ASF virus using appropriate diagnostic tests before integrating them with the existing herd.

 *---------------------------------------* 

3. Pig sourcing: Be cautious about sourcing pigs from areas with known ASF outbreaks or from unknown sources. Purchase pigs only from reputable and ASF-free sources to reduce the risk of introducing the virus into your farm
4/18/23, 3:13 PM - Bamiche: Regarding #2, in the future we're going to need a few dedicated pens for quarantining new pigs
4/18/23, 3:18 PM - Bamiche: also no dogs from outside or any other animal is allowed in the farm

4. Pig transportation: Ensure that vehicles used for pig transportation are properly cleaned and disinfected before and after each use. Avoid using vehicles that have been in contact with pigs from unknown or ASF-infected sources.

----------------------------------

5. Feed and equipment: Use only feed and equipment that are known to be free from ASF virus. Avoid using swill or kitchen waste as pig feed, as it can be a potential source of ASF virus.

----------------------------------
6. Rodent and vector control: Implement effective rodent and vector control measures to prevent them from spreading ASF virus. High fever

- Weakness and difficulty standing

- Vomiting

- Diarrhea , which may be bloody

- Red or blue boils on the skin, particularly around the ears and snout
Laboured breathing and coughing

- Loss of appetite

3/9/25, 3:46 PM - Ezra: Creating rules and regulations for pig a farm is essential for maintaining a safe, efficient, and humane operation. Here are some rules you can consider implementing for your workers:

1.General Conduct and Behavior for workers

Respect and Professionalism: All workers must maintain a respectful and professional attitude towards colleagues, management, and animals at all times.

Cleanliness: Workers are required to keep their assigned areas clean and organized, including pens, equipment, and common areas.

Punctuality: Workers must adhere to their scheduled working hours. Any lateness should be communicated in advance.

Proper Uniform: All workers must wear the required uniform, including gloves, boots, and other safety equipment, when working with animals or equipment

Dedication, interest and passion: All workers must exhibit strong interest, passion and dedication for the job.

No stealing

No fighting/Quarrelling

Visitors are not allowed into the farm

Proper Respect for the management.


General Animal Welfare

Treatment of Animals: Workers are to handle pigs with care and respect at all times, ensuring they are not subjected to unnecessary stress or harm.

Feeding and Watering: All pigs should be fed according to the established schedule, with fresh, clean water available at all times.

Animal Health Monitoring: At all times, workers must check the health conditions of the pigs and report any signs of illness, injury, or abnormal behavior in pigs to the farm supervisor immediately.

Sanitation: Workers are responsible for cleaning and disinfecting animal pens, equipment, and any areas that pigs have contact with, to prevent disease spread. You must ensure that the pens are always clean.

Footbath: Workers and visitors must disinfect their foot before entering the farm.

RECORD KEEPING

Workers must keep accurate and detailed records of each pig's health, growth and breeding history. 

Workers must monitor feed consumption, growth rate, and the weights to access the farm productivity. 


BREEDING/HEAT MANAGEMENT

Breeding and heats are one of the most important aspects of Piggery because if not properly monitored, will lead to food wastage, time waste.

The best time to inseminate a pig is about 12 hours before ovulation which occurs around 36-40 hours after the start of standing heat.

Workers must always take note and observe the heat periods of the pigs…

SIGNS OF HEAT PERIODS OF PIGS

Swollen Vulva
Mounting on each other 
Reddish vulva


Disciplinary Actions

Violation of Rules: Workers who fail to follow farm rules and regulations will be subject to disciplinary action, ranging from verbal warnings to termination, depending on the severity of the violation.

Reporting Violations: All workers are encouraged to report any violations of these rules to management. Confidentiality will be maintained where necessary.

Note: The farm welfare is a collective effort of all the workers. You should not be limited to your work area.
